Well Evaluation
Marathon Oil Company
Victor USA 34-12TFH
Figure 1. H&P #259 drilling the Victor USA 34-12TFH well southwest of
Mandaree, ND on October 12, 2014 (Anna Bruckmeier, Wellsite Geologist)
INTRODUCTION
Marathon Oil Company Victor USA 34-12TFH [SW SE Section 12, T148N, R96W] lies
within Lost Bridge Field and is located approximately 13 miles southwest of Mandaree, North
Dakota in Dunn County. Lost Bridge field has historically produced 365,204 bbls of oil from
Devonian formations and 5,329,108 bbls of oil from the Bakken. The Victor USA 34-12TFH is
the third of four wells completed on this pad within the Williston Basin by H&P #259 for
Marathon Oil Company (Figure 1). The Victor USA 34-12TFH is a double-section horizontal
well drilled to the north (5.06°) within the Three Forks Formation. The vertical portion was
planned to be drilled to a kick-off point of 10,721' within the Lodgepole Formation. Build rates
of 12° per 100' were required to land the curve at approximately 90° within the targeted interval
27' below the base of the Lower Bakken Shale according to the prognosis. Intermediate casing
would then be set and cemented prior to commencing the lateral portion of the well. The lateral
would be drilled to a planned total depth of 20,033' within Lot 1 of Section 1, T148N, R96W
(Figure 2). Upon the completion of the Victor USA 34-12TFH, the hole will be prepared for
casing and production evaluation using 30 staged artificial fracture techniques with external
casing swell packers and sleeves.

OFFSET WELLS
Three primary offsets were used to establish a prognosis of formation tops and thicknesses to be
used as a control for the anticipated structure of the Victor USA 34-12TFH (Figure 3). Offset
formation thicknesses were compared and an appropriate curve landing target was selected based
on the average of these thicknesses. The offsets include:
-Elk Creek USA 33-12H [SW SE Sec. 12, T148N, R96W] shares the same pad as the Victor
USA 34-12TFH. It is a Middle Bakken horizontal that is currently active.
-Buffalo 34-12H [SW SE Sec. 12, T148N, R96W] shares the same pad as the Victor USA 34-
12TFH. It is a Three Forks horizontal that is currently active.
-Deep Creek USA 14-12TFH [NW NW Sec. 13, T148N, R96W] is 0.75 miles south west of the
Victor USA 34-12TFH. It is a Three Forks horizontal that is currently active.
Offset dip profiles from the Deep Creek USA 14-12TFH and the Elk Creek USA 33-12H were
used for structure control during horizontal drilling.
Figure 3. Marathon Oil Company Victor USA 34-12TFH and surrounding offset wells
(NDIC Oil and Gas Division, Arc IMS online)
ENGINEERING OPERATIONS
Surface/Vertical
Drilling rig H&P #259 spud the Victor USA 34-12TFH on September 26, 2014 with fresh water
and a 12 ¼" tri cone bit that drilled 2,247' in 4 drilling hours. Surface casing 9 5/8" in diameter
(36# J-55) was set to a depth of 2,335'and cemented in place. The fresh water was then displaced
with diesel invert drilling mud weighted 9.45-10.40ppg for the vertical and curve portions of the
well. Vertical operations were completed with two 8 ¾" PDC bits that drilled to a total depth of
10,628'. An inclination of approximately 3 degrees and an azimuth of approximately 140
degrees were maintained in order to walk the well bore to the southeast and gain vertical section
before lateral drilling commenced. The vertical portion of the well was completed on October 2,
2014 at 00:00 CDT with both bits totaling 8,276' in 100.1 hours.
Curve Build
Directional and MWD services were provided by Pat's Consulting and Scientific Drilling
International. A fixed 2.38° mud motor and 8 ¾" PDC bit were tripped in the hole at 10,628' for
the curve build section. The curve was drilled to a measured depth of 11,099' and the decision
was made to trip for a new MWD tool and a more aggressive bit. An 8 ¾ tri cone bit and fixed
2.38° mud motor were then tripped in the hole. The curve was then drilled to a measured depth
of 11,193. Slides were still not yielding proper build rates and the decision was made to trip
again for a more aggressive assembly. An 8 ¾" tri cone bit and 3.00° adjustable mud motor were
tripped in the hole. The curve was drilled to a total depth of 11,520' at 18:05 CDT on October 5,
2014; a total of 892' in 34.3 drilling hours. Necessary build rates were not achieved and the
curve was landed 14' below the target. Seven inch intermediate casing, consisting of 32# L-80
was set to a depth of 11,504' and cemented.
Lateral
Diesel invert drilling fluid was displaced with salt water for the duration of the lateral with a
density of 9.7-10 ppg. Drilling of the lateral hole began on October 8, 2014 at a depth of 11,520'
with a 6" PDC bit, 1.5° fixed bend mud motor, and Scientific MWD tools for surveys and
gamma data. After drilling 8,249' in 55 drilling hours to a depth of 19,769', the mud motor failed
and the decision was made to trip out of the hole. A new 6" bit, 1.5° fixed bend mud motor, and
MWD tools were subsequently tripped in the hole. The new assembly drilled 406' to a total
depth of 20,175' MD in 2.8 drilling hours. Total depth was reached on October 13, 2014 at 04:20
CDT with a closure azimuth of 5.17° and a closure distance of 8,607.91'. The bottom-hole
location (BHL) is estimated to be 8,572.94' north and 775.13' east of surface location or
approximately 215.18' FNL & 678.87' FEL, Lot 1 Section 1, T148N, R96W in Dunn County,
North Dakota.
GEOLOGIC EVALUATION
Methods
Sunburst Consulting, Inc. provided well site geologic supervision for the Victor USA 34-12TFH.
A two-person team of geologists provided geo-steering services as well as logged cuttings and
monitored gas from 8,700 until the well was drilled to completion. A digital gas detection system
and chromatograph provided by Mudlogging Systems, Inc. were interfaced with the Pason
electronic data recording system (EDR), which provided drilling parameters to the MControl
program as well as displayed total gas data accessible around location. Total mud gas data were
measured and recorded in units (100 units = 1% methane equivalent in air) and measured
component concentrations of methane, ethane, propane, and butane in parts per million. Rock
cuttings were collected by rig crews in 30' lagged samples under the supervision of the well site
geologists. The cuttings were then examined wet and dry using a 10x-35x zoom binocular stereo
microscope with 10x oculars. These data, in conjunction with gamma ray data provided by the
Scientific MWDs and real-time drilling parameters from the Pason EDR, were used to provide
the directional team with optimal TVD targets ensuring the wellbore would achieve maximum
contact within the targeted drilling interval.
Prospective Pay Zones and Hydrocarbon Shows
Note: There were no electric logs run for the Victor USA 34-12TFH; therefore, all depths while
drilling the vertical and curve are referenced to driller's depth. A complete listing of sample
descriptions is provided in the appendix of this report.
The Mission Canyon Formation [Mississippian; Madison Group] was seen at a depth of 9,672'
MD [9,660 TVD, (-7,143' subsea)]. The Mission Canyon is characterized by a transition from
argillaceous and dolomitic limestone to a cleaner limestone. The strata in the upper portion of the
Mission Canyon are marked by several layers of anhydrite and dolomite interbedded with
limestone. Samples consisted primarily of mudstone and rarely wackestone that were light gray
to light brown in color and occasionally argillaceous. Trace amounts of intercrystalline porosity
and dark brown spotty oil staining were noted in the middle and lower portions of the formation
which were accompanied by hydrocarbon shows of 89 units (9,820' MD), 122 units (9,945' MD)
and 114 units (10,105'MD) and background gas averaging between 50 and 60 units.
The Lodgepole Formation [Mississippian; Madison Group] was encountered at a depth of
10,227' MD [10,214' TVD (-7,697' subsea)] and marked by a transition from clean limestone to
argillaceous limestone, predominately mudstone. Samples were primarily gray brown in color
with trace amounts of disseminated pyrite and no visible porosity or oil staining observed. There
was one significant hydrocarbon show, most likely a result of fracture porosity, seen at 10,929'
MD and reaching 375 units. Background gas averaged 20 units and increased to 50 units in the
lower portion of the formation, and a trip gas of 452 units was seen at 11,099' MD. The lower
20' of the Lodgepole is characterized by two informal strata: the False Bakken and the
underlying Scallion interval. The False Bakken is a dark gray calcareous shale that has a 95 unit
hydrocarbon show associated with it at 11,122' MD. The Scallion is a gray brown limestone with
no visible porosity.
The Upper Shale Member of the Bakken Formation [Mississippian] was logged at a depth of
11,140' MD [11,098' TVD (-8,581' subsea)] with sample returns consisting of hard, black,
carbonaceous and petroliferous shale that was calcareous in part and had common disseminated
and nodular pyrite. The penetration of the shale was accompanied by a higher gamma ray
signature, faster drilling rates, and increased hydrocarbon shows; specifically a show of 180 units
at 11,162' MD. Due to the inclination at which this interval was encountered, there was very
limited exposure (27'.) The Middle Bakken Member [Devonian-Mississippian] was logged at a
depth of 11,167' MD [11,117' TVD (-8,600' subsea)] with sample returns consisting of light
gray brown, very fine grained, silty sandstone that is calcite and occasionally dolomite cemented
and has trace amounts of disseminated pyrite. The upper portion of the Middle Bakken is
characterized by a gray, calcareous, siltstone underlain by a thin layer of packstone, noted by a
significant decrease in gamma ray values. The Middle Bakken Member is also characterized by
its poor permeability and porosity, making it an unconventional reservoir, which is remedied by
the hydraulic fracturing process. Trace amounts of intergranular porosity and light brown spotty
oil staining were observed and accompanied by a hydrocarbon show of 152 units at 11,185' MD.
Background gas averaged 60 units for the duration of this interval with a trip gas of 133 units at
11,193' MD. The Lower Shale Member was logged at a depth of 11,220' MD [11,160' TVD
(-8,643' subsea)] with sample returns of dark brown to black carbonaceous and petroliferous
shale similar to the Upper Bakken member. It is also characterized by faster drilling rates, higher
gamma ray signature, and increased hydrocarbon shows. Background gas averaged around 80
units with a show of 139 units at 11,234' MD. The Pronghorn Member [Devonian] was seen at a
depth of 11,262' MD [11,183' TVD (-8,666' subsea) and is characterized by interbedded dark
gray, hard siltstone and light gray brown limestone. Rare to occasional amounts of disseminated
and nodular pyrite were also observed. Light brown spotty oil staining was accompanied by a
186 unit hydrocarbon show at 11,275' MD.
The Three Forks Formation [Devonian] was logged at a depth of 11,290' MD [11,201' TVD
(-8,684'subsea)] with sample returns of pale mint green shale, off white and light brown sandy
dolomite and trace amounts of a light gray dolomite cemented sandstone. Pyrite is seen
throughout the formation, most commonly in the euhedral form in the shale and occasionally as
disseminated and nodular in the shale and dolomite. No visible porosity was observed in the
shale intervals. Rare spotty to even oil staining and intercrystalline porosity were both observed
in the dolomite intervals. The targeted zone was 12' thick and described as:
DOLOMITE: mudstone, off white to light brown, microcrystalline, friable to firm, sucrosic
texture, sandy in part, trace to rare disseminated pyrite, trace intercrystalline porosity,
rare spotty to even dark brown oil stain; occasional SHALE: pale mint green, friable,
earthy texture, rare to occasional euhedral pyrite, trace disseminated pyrite; very trace
SANDSTONE: off white to light gray, very fine grained, firm to friable, sub angular to sub
round, moderately sorted, dolomitic cement, trace disseminated pyrite, possible
intergranular porosity.
Figure 4. Three Forks shale and sandy dolomite from the targeted interval.
Lateral Hydrocarbon Shows
Lateral hydrocarbon shows were highest in the lower half of zone, particularly between the base
of target and the chocolate dolomite, most likely due to the predominately sandy dolomite layer
just below the base of zone. Due to increasing connection gasses the decision was made to begin
circulating through the gas buster at 14,047' MD. Prior to that, background gas averaged 500
units and increased to 800 units with connection gasses approaching 2,000 units just before
circulation through the gas buster began (Figure 5). An intermittent flare of 1-5' was observed
and slowly transitioned to a constant flare by the end of the lateral. Gas components C1-C4 were
observed throughout the course of the lateral. Once circulation through the gas buster began,
average background gas dropped to 100-400 units with connection gasses averaging between 200
and 400 units. No back pressure was held while drilling the Victor USA 34-12TFH.

Geo-steering
Day tour directional services and well-site supervision were provided by RPM Consulting for the
lateral portion of the well. Scientific Drilling International provided day directional services
through the vertical and curve and night directional and MWD services throughout the duration
of the well. Sunburst Consulting, Inc well-site geologists worked in conjunction with the
directional drillers, MWDs, and the prospect geologist to make decisions ensuring maximum
wellbore exposure within the targeted zone.
The prognosis called for a landing target of 11,213' TVD or 27' below the base of the Lower
Bakken Shale which would put the well bore in the center of target at approximately 90 degrees.
The three primary offsets used for gamma correlation through vertical and curve were the
Buffalo 34-12H and the Elk Creek USA 33-12H which both share the same pad as the Victor
USA 34-12TFH, and the Deep Creek USA 14-12H which is less than a mile away. Real time
gamma ray data obtained from the MWDs was used to correlate formation thicknesses between
the Victor USA 34-12TFH and its offsets. Based on these correlations the landing target was
kept at 11,213' TVD through curve landing. Due to issues maintaining proper build rates the
curve was landed 14' below the landing target at 11,227' TVD. The Singalness 2-10 was used as
the thickness analog well for the target and a type log was created with the top of target coming
in 30' below the base of the Lower Bakken Shale at 11,213' TVD and the base at 11,225' TVD
(Figure 6). The targeted interval was 12' thick contained markers E-H.
Figure 6. Type log from curve landing with Marathon Oil Company Victor USA 34-12TFH in red and the
Singalness 2-10 in black.
The lateral began with a fair amount of sliding as a result of drilling out of the casing shoe at a
higher than expected inclination. Based on the measured depths at which various gamma markers
were encountered, local structure dip estimates were determined and TVD targets were provided
accordingly to the directional team. The "H" marker located at the base of the targeted interval
proved most useful in determining these dip estimates. The offset profiles from the Deep Creek
21-13TFH and Elk Creek USA 33-12H were used for structure control since both wells parallel
the Victor USA 34-12TFH. These data, in conjunction with samples and gas data, were used to
steer and ensure maximum exposure to the targeted interval. Dips averaged flat for the majority
of the lateral with dip estimates between +0.33 to -0.25; however, the last 2,000' of the lateral
saw an approximate down dip of 0.34 which, in turn, led to a gross apparent down dip of 0.06
over the course of the entire lateral (Figure 7). The wellbore exited the top of the target interval
on three occasions and the base of the target on four occasions for a total of 2,257' making the
overall percentage drilled in zone 74% or 6,588'.

SUMMARY
The Victor USA 34-12TFH is a Three Forks horizontal well successfully drilled in Lost Bridge
Field in 17 days, reaching a TD of 20,175' on October 13, 2014. Samples from the Three Forks
pay zone consisted of a pale mint green shale, an off white to light brown sandy dolomite with
sucrosic texture and spotty to even oil staining and trace amounts of a light gray dolomite
cemented sandstone, all with varying abundances of pyrite. Background gas values were 500-800
units during the first portion of the lateral and decreased to 200-400 units once circulation
through the gas buster began. A flare of 1'-5' was observed and no back pressure was held. The
overall apparent dip of the Victor USA 34-12TFH was approximately 0.06° down. The wellbore
remained in the target zone for 74% of the lateral, exposing 6,588' to the pay zone. The Victor
USA 34-12TFH is awaiting completion operations to maximize production.
Respectfully submitted,
Anna Bruckmeier
Sunburst Consulting, Inc.

LITHOLOGY
Marathon Oil Company ­ Victor USA 34-12TFH
Rig crews caught lagged samples in 30' intervals under the supervision of Sunburst geologists. A detailed list of
sampling intervals is included in the well data summary page. Sample or gamma ray marker tops have been
inserted in the sample descriptions below for reference. Samples were examined wet and dry under a binocular
microscope. The drilling fluid was diesel-based invert from surface casing to 11,520' and changed to salt-water
from 11,520' to 20,175' TD. Sample collection began at 8,700'.
Vertical
Kibbey "Lime"
8,709' MD; 8,700' TVD (-6,183')
8700-8730 SILTY SANDSTONE: light brown, light to medium gray, occasional red to brown, firm, sub blocky, calcareous
cement, poorly cemented, occasional ANHYDRITE: off white to cream, microcrystalline, firm to soft, massive, amorphous
8730-8760 LIMESTONE: mudstone, light gray brown, microcrystalline, firm to friable, earthy texture; SILTSTONE: light to
medium gray, light brown, occasional light red to brown, firm, sub blocky, calcareous cement, poorly cemented
8760-8790 SILTSTONE: light to medium gray, light rounded brown, light orange brown, firm, sub blocky, calcareous
cement, poorly cemented
8790-8820 SILTSTONE: light to medium gray, light rounded brown, light orange brown, firm, sub blocky, calcareous
cement, poorly cemented
8820-8850 SILTSTONE: light to medium gray, light rounded brown, light orange brown, firm, sub blocky, calcareous
cement, poorly cemented

RE:
HORIZONTAL WELL
VICTOR USA 34-12TFH
SWSE Section 12-148N-96W
Dunn County
Well File # 29003
Dear William:
Pursuant to Commission Order No. 24318, approval to drill the above captioned well is hereby given. The approval is granted on
the condition that all portions of the well bore not isolated by cement, be no closer than the 200' setback from the north & south
boundaries and 500' setback from the east & west boundaries within the 2560 acre spacing unit consisting of Sections 1, 12, 13 & 24
T148N R96W. Tool error is not required pursuant to order.
PERMIT STIPULATIONS: Effective June 1, 2014, a covered leak-proof container (with placard) for filter sock disposal must be
maintained on the well site beginning when the well is spud, and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-
back whenever filtration operations are conducted.
Due to drainage adjacent to the well site, a dike is required surrounding
the entire location.
All distances on the Production Layout Plat must comply with NDAC 43-02-03-28 (SAFETY
REGULATION). MARATHON OIL COMPANY must take into consideration NDAC 43-02-03-28 (Safety Regulation) when
contemplating simultaneous operations on the above captioned location. Pursuant to NDAC 43-02-03-28 (Safety Regulation)
"No boiler, portable electric lighting generator, or treater shall be placed nearer than 150 feet to any producing well or oil tank."
MARATHON OIL CO must contact NDIC Field Inspector Joyce Kohut at 701-202-1288 prior to location construction.
Drilling pit
NDAC 43-02-03-19.4 states that "a pit may be utilized to bury drill cuttings and solids generated during well drilling and completion
operations, providing the pit can be constructed, used and reclaimed in a manner that will prevent pollution of the land surface and
freshwaters. Reserve and circulation of mud system through earthen pits are prohibited. All pits shall be inspected by an authorized
representative of the director prior to lining and use. Drill cuttings and solids must be stabilized in a manner approved by the director
prior to placement in a cuttings pit."
Form 1 Changes & Hard Lines
Any changes, shortening of casing point or lengthening at Total Depth must have prior approval by the NDIC. The proposed directional
plan is at a legal location. Based on the azimuth of the proposed lateral the maximum legal coordinate from the well head is: 8589'N and
954'E.
Location Construction Commencement (Three Day Waiting Period)
Operators shall not commence operations on a drill site until the 3rd business day following publication of the approved drilling permit
on the NDIC - OGD Daily Activity Report. If circumstances require operations to commence before the 3rd business day following
publication on the Daily Activity Report, the waiting period may be waived by the Director. Application for a waiver must be by sworn
affidavit providing the information necessary to evaluate the extenuating circumstances, the factors of NDAC 43-02-03-16.2 (1), (a)-(f), and
any other information that would allow the Director to conclude that in the event another owner seeks revocation of the drilling permit,
the applicant should retain the permit.
Permit Fee & Notification
Payment was received in the amount of $100 via credit card. It is requested that notification be given immediately upon the
spudding of the well. This information should be relayed to the Oil & Gas Division, Bismarck, via telephone. The following information
must be included: Well name, legal location, permit number, drilling contractor, company representative, date and time of spudding.
Office hours are 8:00 a.m. to 12:00 p.m. and 1:00 p.m. to 5:00 p.m. Central Time. Our telephone number is (701) 328-8020, leave a
message if after hours or on the weekend.
William F Groffy
July 30, 2014
Page 2
Survey Requirements for Horizontal, Horizontal Re-entry, and Directional Wells
NDAC Section 43-02-03-25 (Deviation Tests and Directional Surveys) states in part (that) the survey contractor shall file a certified
copy of all surveys with the director free of charge within thirty days of completion. Surveys must be submitted as one electronic copy, or
in a form approved by the director. However, the director may require the directional survey to be filed immediately after completion if the
survey is needed to conduct the operation of the director's office in a timely manner. Certified surveys must be submitted via email in one
adobe document, with a certification cover page to certsurvey@nd.gov.
Survey points shall be of such frequency to accurately determine the entire location of the well bore.
Specifically, the Horizontal and Directional well survey frequency is 100 feet in the vertical, 30 feet in the curve (or when sliding) and 90
feet in the lateral.
Confidential status
Your request for confidential status of all information furnished to the Director, or his representatives, is hereby granted. Such
information, except production runs, shall remain confidential for six months commencing on the date the well is spud.
Confidential status notwithstanding, the Director and his representatives shall have access to all well records wherever located.
Your company personnel, or any person performing work for your company shall permit the Director and his representatives to come
upon any lease, property, well, or drilling rig operated or controlled by them, complying with all safety rules, and to inspect the records and
operation of such wells and to have access at all times to any and all records of wells. The Commission's field personnel periodically inspect
producing and drilling wells. Any information regarding such wells shall be made available to them at any time upon request. The
information so obtained by the field personnel shall be maintained in strict confidence and shall be available only to the Commission and
its staff.
Surface casing cement
Tail cement utilized on surface casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi within 12 hours, and tail cement
utilized on production casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi before drilling the plug or initiating tests.
Logs
NDAC Section 43-02-03-31 requires the running of (1) a suite of open hole logs from which formation tops and porosity zones
can be determined, (2) a Gamma Ray Log run from total depth to ground level elevation of the well bore, and (3) a log from which the
presence and quality of cement can be determined (Standard CBL or Ultrasonic cement evaluation log) in every well in which production
or intermediate casing has been set, this log must be run prior to completing the well. All logs run must be submitted free of charge, as
one digital TIFF (tagged image file format) copy and one digital LAS (log ASCII) formatted copy. Digital logs may be submitted on a
standard CD, DVD, or attached to an email sent to digitallogs@nd.gov Thank you for your cooperation.

Alice Webber

Engineering Tech
April 9, 2014
RE:
Filter Socks and Other Filter Media
Leakproof Container Required
Oil and Gas Wells
Dear Operator,
North Dakota Administrative Code Section 43-02-03-19.2 states in part that all waste material associated with
exploration or production of oil and gas must be properly disposed of in an authorized facility in accord with all
applicable local, state, and federal laws and regulations.
Filtration systems are commonly used during oil and gas operations in North Dakota. The Commission is very
concerned about the proper disposal of used filters (including filter socks) used by the oil and gas industry.
Effective June 1, 2014, a container must be maintained on each well drilled in North Dakota beginning when the
well is spud and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations
are conducted. The on-site container must be used to store filters until they can be properly disposed of in an
authorized facility. Such containers must be:
leakproof to prevent any fluids from escaping the container
covered to prevent precipitation from entering the container
placard to indicate only filters are to be placed in the container
If the operator will not utilize a filtration system, a waiver to the container requirement will be considered, but
only upon the operator submitting a Sundry Notice (Form 4) justifying their request.
As previously stated in our March 13, 2014 letter, North Dakota Administrative Code Section 33-20-02.1-01
states in part that every person who transports solid waste (which includes oil and gas exploration and production
wastes) is required to have a valid permit issued by the North Dakota Department of Health, Division of Waste
Management. Please contact the Division of Waste Management at (701) 328-5166 with any questions on the
solid waste program. Note oil and gas exploration and production wastes include produced water, drilling mud,
invert mud, tank bottom sediment, pipe scale, filters, and fly ash.
Thank you for your cooperation.
Sincerely,
Bruce E. Hicks
Assistant Director
Marathon Oil Company

1.
BOP EQUIPMENT
Marathon Oil Company's minimum specifications for pressure
control equipment are as follows:
Ram Type:
13 5/8" 5000 psi blind, pipe and annular.
a. Due to Marathon's experience it is felt that the above
referenced BOP equipment is adequate for drilling this well.
The reduced permeability of the target zone along with
Marathon's area experience of drilling over 150 horizontal
wells indicate that a MASP of 3000 psi is more adjusted to
the reality of the reservoir.
BOP and other equipment testing:
a. Floor valve, dart valve, kill valves, check valve, manual
choke line valve, manual top drive valve, hydraulic top
drive valve, HCR, choke house valves, choke manifold,
choke hose, choke line, kill line, upper pipe rams, lower
pipe rams, blind rams (Low Test: 250 psi x 5 min. High
Test: 5000 psi x 10 min.)
b. Annular Preventer (Low Test: 250 psi x 5 min. High Test:
2500 psi x 10 min.)
c. Rotating head and Orbit Valve (Low Test: 250 psi x 5 min.
High Test: 1500 psi x 10 min.)
Frequency:
a. After initial installation (NU BOPE).
b. Whenever any seal subject to test pressure is broken.
c. After any repairs compromising seal.
d. At 30-day intervals.
All other equipment (upper and lower Kelly cocks, IBOP,
etc) will be tested according to Onshore Oil and Gas
Order No. 2.

EVALUATION PROGRAM
The anticipated type and amount of testing, logging and coring
are as follows:
a. The logging program will consist of the following:
i. Waiver is attached not to run logs except those
shown below.
ii. CBL to be run above cement top and a GR back to
surface.
iii. Curve will be drilled with MWD including GR to
intermediate casing point.
b. Mud logging services will commence prior to penetrating
below (base of Charles salt):
i. Samples will be obtained at 10' intervals to
intermediate casing point and at 30' intervals below
intermediate to TD.
c. No drill stem tests are anticipated.

5.
ABNORMAL PRESSURES AND H2S GAS
a. The maximum anticipated bottom-hole pressure is 7810 psi.
Abnormal pressures are not anticipated.
b. Potential exists for hydrogen sulfide gas in the Madison.
6.
Well Completion
a. A 4 ½" liner will be run from above the 7" casing shoe to
the bottom of the well.
Liner has frac sleeves
installed.
b. Tie back liner will be run from top of 4 ½" Liner back to
the surface.
c. Well will be fractured utilizing a 30 stage frac.
d. Pursuant to NDIC letter effective February 12,2014,
concerning Hydraulic Fracture Stimulation using Diesel
Fuels, Marathon Oil Company will not inject diesel fuel
or any diesel-type chemicals (68334-30-5, 68476-34-6,
68476-30-2, 68476-31-3, or 8008-20-6) during the
hydraulic fracture stimulation process or this well.
Marathon understands the guidelines that are outline in
the above referenced letter including the requirement to
obtain an Underground Injection Control, Class II permit
from the NDIC prior to commencing any Hydraulic Fracture
Stimulation in which any amount of diesel fuel or any
diesel type chemical is injected.

street address for this well per the requirements in NDAC 43-02-03-16.
